<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Mathematical operation</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Exponent" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Exponent_(disambiguation)" title="Exponent (disambiguation)">Exponent (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox" style="max-width:20em;"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-above" colspan="2" style="background: #ccc; font-size: 500%; line-height:1.3; font-weight:normal; font-family:'times new roman', times, georgia, serif;"><span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span></th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2" style="background: #ccc;"><div style="background: #ccc; font-size: 125%; font-weight: bold; padding: 0.1em 0.25em 0.2em; line-height: 1.2em;">notation</div></th></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2">base b and exponent n</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:317px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Expo02.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Expo02.svg/315px-Expo02.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Expo02.svg/473px-Expo02.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Expo02.svg/630px-Expo02.svg.png 2x" width="315"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Expo02.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphs of <span class="texhtml"><i>y</i> = <i>b</i><sup><i>x</i></sup></span> for various bases <i>b</i>: <span class="nowrap"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><span class="legend" style="padding-right:5px;"><span class="legend-line mw-no-invert" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 1.67em; height: 0; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted black;border-top:green solid 2px;"> </span> <a href="#Powers_of_ten">base 10</a>,</span></span> <span class="nowrap"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend" style="padding-right:5px;"><span class="legend-line mw-no-invert" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 1.67em; height: 0; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted black;border-top:red solid 2px;"> </span> <a href="#The_exponential_function">base <i>e</i></a>,</span></span> <span class="nowrap"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend" style="padding-right:5px;"><span class="legend-line mw-no-invert" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 1.67em; height: 0; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted black;border-top:blue solid 2px;"> </span> <a href="#Powers_of_two">base 2</a>,</span></span> <span class="nowrap"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="legend" style="padding-right:5px;"><span class="legend-line mw-no-invert" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 1.67em; height: 0; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted black;border-top:cyan solid 2px;"> </span> base <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1050945101">.mw-parser-output .sfrac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .sfrac.tion,.mw-parser-output .sfrac .tion{display:inline-block;vertical-align:-0.5em;font-size:85%;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .num,.mw-parser-output .sfrac .den{display:block;line-height:1em;margin:0 0.1em}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .den{border-top:1px solid}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="sfrac tion" role="math"><span class="num">1</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den">2</span></span>.</span></span> Each curve passes through the point <span class="texhtml">(0, 1)</span> because any nonzero number raised to the power of 0 is 1. At <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i> = 1</span>, the value of <i>y</i> equals the base because any number raised to the power of 1 is the number itself.</div></div></div>

</tr></tbody></table></div>
<p><b>Exponentiation</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematical</a> <a href="/wiki/Operation_(mathematics)" title="Operation (mathematics)">operation</a>, written as <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span>, involving two numbers, the <i><a href="/wiki/Base_(exponentiation)" title="Base (exponentiation)">base</a></i> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span> and the <i>exponent</i> or <i>power</i> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>, and pronounced as "<span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span> (raised) to the (power of) <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">[1]</a></sup> When <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> is a positive <a href="/wiki/Integer" title="Integer">integer</a>, exponentiation corresponds to repeated <a href="/wiki/Multiplication" title="Multiplication">multiplication</a> of the base: that is, <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Product_(mathematics)" title="Product (mathematics)">product</a> of multiplying <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> bases:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{n}=\underbrace {b\times b\times \dots \times b\times b} _{n{\text{ times}}}.}" display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<munder>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OP MJX-fixedlimits">
<munder>
<mrow>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mo>⋯<!-- ⋯ --></mo>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>×<!-- × --></mo>
<mi>b</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>⏟<!-- ⏟ --></mo>
</munder>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext> times</mtext>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</munder>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{n}=\underbrace {b\times b\times \dots \times b\times b} _{n{\text{ times}}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></div><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{n}=\underbrace {b\times b\times \dots \times b\times b} _{n{\text{ times}}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dcb8949e2c2dbe952c87d89e208b8018f107ad79" style="vertical-align: -3.671ex; width:24.036ex; height:5.676ex;"/></div></dd></dl>
<p>The exponent is usually shown as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superscript" title="Superscript">superscript</a> to the right of the base. In that case, <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span> is called "<i>b</i> raised to the <i>n</i>th power", "<i>b</i> (raised) to the power of <i>n</i>", "the <i>n</i>th power of <i>b</i>", "<i>b</i> to the <i>n</i>th power",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> or most briefly as "<i>b</i> to the <i>n</i>th".
</p><p>Starting from the basic fact stated above that, for any positive integer <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

In particular:
</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}b^{n+m}&amp;=\underbrace {b\times \dots \times b} _{n+m{\text{ times}}}\\[1ex]&amp;=\underbrace {b\times \dots \times b} _{n{\text{ times}}}\times \underbrace {b\times \dots \times b} _{m{\text{ times}}}\\[1ex]&amp;=b^{n}\times b^{m}\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>In other words, when multiplying a base raised to one exponent by the same base raised to another exponent, the exponents add. From this basic rule that exponents add, we can derive that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{0}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b^{0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b5456c9d8bf077b24d003cf08da7a63403e24a8c" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.052ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> must be equal to 1, as follows. For any <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Dividing both sides by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>The fact that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{1}=b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

For example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (b^{1})^{3}=b^{1}\cdot b^{1}\cdot b^{1}=b^{1+1+1}=b^{3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p><p>The rule that multiplying makes exponents add can also be used to derive the properties of 
negative integer exponents. Consider the question of what <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{-1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b^{-1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0bd13a08ad908dbc733a2137cb105f45a54962b7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.33ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> should mean. In order to respect the "exponents add" rule, it must be the case that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{-1}\cdot b^{1}=b^{-1+1}=b^{0}=1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Dividing both sides by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{-1}=1/b^{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{-1}=1/b^{1}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{-1}=1/b^{1}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/03c40484b8bdab88059d4d0c776d04c5779dca63" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.806ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>, which can be more simply written as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{-1}=1/b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{-1}=1/b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{-1}=1/b}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/13577ab67f579e9c2901142ec86c85665a74e710" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.751ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>, using the result from above that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{1}=b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{1}=b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b^{1}=b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7d240dbaf6181ae1801474f3d28dcd5504aacae6" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.148ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>. By a similar argument, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{-n}=1/b^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{-n}=1/b^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{-n}=1/b^{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2bc089b4a3b2678e49e8a5edef0b8ac3d148f631" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.134ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>The properties of fractional exponents also follow from the same rule. For example, suppose we consider <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>b</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\sqrt{b}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/966599cfadf3cfc0a89e4bf9adb62efbdb0d183a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.933ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> and ask if there is some suitable exponent,  which we may call <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>r</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{r}={\sqrt {b}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>r</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>b</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{r}={\sqrt {b}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{r}={\sqrt {b}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/182d1845dec821db0c1a2380f674097178dc15d1" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.003ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>. From the definition of the square root, we have that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}\cdot {\sqrt {b}}=b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>b</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>b</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}\cdot {\sqrt {b}}=b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}\cdot {\sqrt {b}}=b}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3c0df34c1777631175a3d32597163255a9c62a33" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.642ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>. Therefore, the exponent <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>r</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> must be such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{r}\cdot b^{r}=b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>r</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>r</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{r}\cdot b^{r}=b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{r}\cdot b^{r}=b}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c372ceae3b76f9c9fd334fb71517422afdeec068" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:9.718ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>. Using the fact that multiplying makes exponents add gives <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{r+r}=b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>

<mi>r</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>r</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{r+r}=b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{r+r}=b}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fb0d50b784036a4c6b170a86ce7daa59f8267fef" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.087ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>. The 
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.998ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> on the right-hand side can also be written as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{1}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{1}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f8fb113f055826c4812ce940c24d0f17e2bc69a8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.052ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>, giving <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{r+r}=b^{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>r</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>r</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{r+r}=b^{1}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{r+r}=b^{1}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4c5f432d87e450dc15408d5623f7dbcffdb4acb7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:9.142ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>. Equating the exponents on both sides, we have <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r+r=1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>r</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>r</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r+r=1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle r+r=1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7a5fe0cf1b788638d7ce49670c09ab08f247f5c0" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:9.199ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>. Therefore, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r={\frac {1}{2}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>r</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<mn>2</mn>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r={\frac {1}{2}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="r={\frac {1}{2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bec1c0f5b9b74e4009c1512a293bb72f08dfcde5" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:6.146ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span>, so <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}=b^{\frac {1}{2}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>b</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<mn>2</mn>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}=b^{\frac {1}{2}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {b}}=b^{\frac {1}{2}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2c495d0c5163d124e75fac8661bc1dc5c6d8d87e" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.765ex; height:3.843ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>The definition of exponentiation can be extended to allow any real or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Complex_numbers" title="Complex numbers">complex</a> exponent. Exponentiation by integer exponents can also be defined for a wide variety of algebraic structures, including <a href="/wiki/Matrix_(mathematics)" title="Matrix (mathematics)">matrices</a>.
</p><p>Exponentiation is used extensively in many fields, including <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>, with applications such as <a href="/wiki/Compound_interest" title="Compound interest">compound interest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical_reaction_kinetics" title="Chemical reaction kinetics">chemical reaction kinetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wave" title="Wave">wave</a> behavior, and <a href="/wiki/Public-key_cryptography" title="Public-key cryptography">public-key cryptography</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_the_notation">History of the notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History of the notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The term <i>power</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">potentia, potestas, dignitas</i>) is a mistranslation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rotman_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rotman-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">ancient Greek</a> δύναμις (<i>dúnamis</i>, here: "amplification"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rotman_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rotman-3">[3]</a></sup>) used by the <a href="/wiki/Greek_mathematics" title="Greek mathematics">Greek</a> mathematician <a href="/wiki/Euclid" title="Euclid">Euclid</a> for the square of a line,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacTutor_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-MacTutor-5">[5]</a></sup> following <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates_of_Chios" title="Hippocrates of Chios">Hippocrates of Chios</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sand_Reckoner" title="The Sand Reckoner">The Sand Reckoner</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Archimedes" title="Archimedes">Archimedes</a> discovered and proved the law of exponents, <span class="texhtml">10<sup><i>a</i></sup> · 10<sup><i>b</i></sup> = 10<sup><i>a</i>+<i>b</i></sup></span>, necessary to manipulate powers of <span class="texhtml">10</span>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the 9th century, the Persian mathematician <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_M%C5%ABs%C4%81_al-Khw%C4%81rizm%C4%AB" title="Muhammad ibn Mūsā al-Khwārizmī">Muhammad ibn Mūsā al-Khwārizmī</a> used the terms مَال (<i>māl</i>, "possessions", "property") for a <a href="/wiki/Square_(algebra)" title="Square (algebra)">square</a>—the Muslims, "like most mathematicians of those and earlier times, thought of a squared number as a depiction of an area, especially of land, hence property"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldwidewords_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldwidewords-7">[7]</a></sup>—and كَعْبَة (<i><a href="/wiki/Kaaba" title="Kaaba">kaʿbah</a></i>, "cube") for a <a href="/wiki/Cube_(algebra)" title="Cube (algebra)">cube</a>, which later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mathematics_in_medieval_Islam" title="Mathematics in medieval Islam">Islamic</a> mathematicians represented in <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_notation" title="Mathematical notation">mathematical notation</a> as the letters <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C4%ABm" title="Mīm">mīm</a></i> (m) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C4%81f" title="Kāf">kāf</a></i> (k), respectively, by the 15th century, as seen in the work of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ab%C5%AB_al-Hasan_ibn_Al%C4%AB_al-Qalas%C4%81d%C4%AB" title="Abū al-Hasan ibn Alī al-Qalasādī">Abū al-Hasan ibn Alī al-Qalasādī</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Jost_B%C3%BCrgi" title="Jost Bürgi">Jost Bürgi</a> used Roman numerals for exponents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cajori_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-cajori-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Chuquet" title="Nicolas Chuquet">Nicolas Chuquet</a> used a form of exponential notation in the 15th century, which was later used by <a href="/wiki/Henricus_Grammateus" title="Henricus Grammateus">Henricus Grammateus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Stifel" title="Michael Stifel">Michael Stifel</a> in the 16th century. The word <i>exponent</i> was coined in 1544 by Michael Stifel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Jeake" title="Samuel Jeake">Samuel Jeake</a> introduced the term <i>indices</i> in 1696.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MacTutor_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-MacTutor-5">[5]</a></sup> In the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Recorde" title="Robert Recorde">Robert Recorde</a> used the terms square, cube, zenzizenzic (<a href="/wiki/Fourth_power" title="Fourth power">fourth power</a>), sursolid (fifth), zenzicube (sixth), second sursolid (seventh), and <a href="/wiki/Zenzizenzizenzic" title="Zenzizenzizenzic">zenzizenzizenzic</a> (eighth).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldwidewords_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-worldwidewords-7">[7]</a></sup> <i>Biquadrate</i> has been used to refer to the fourth power as well.
</p><p>Early in the 17th century, the first form of our modern exponential notation was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Descartes" title="René Descartes">René Descartes</a> in his text titled <i><a href="/wiki/La_G%C3%A9om%C3%A9trie" title="La Géométrie">La Géométrie</a></i>; there, the notation is introduced in Book I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some mathematicians (such as <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>) used exponents only for powers greater than two, preferring to represent squares as repeated multiplication. Thus they would write <a href="/wiki/Polynomial" title="Polynomial">polynomials</a>, for example, as <span class="texhtml"><i>ax</i> + <i>bxx</i> + <i>cx</i><sup>3</sup> + <i>d</i></span>.
</p><p>Another historical synonym,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="synonym of what? (August 2021)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <b>involution</b>, is now rare<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and should not be confused with <a href="/wiki/Involution_(mathematics)" title="Involution (mathematics)">its more common meaning</a>.
</p><p>
In 1748, <a href="/wiki/Leonhard_Euler" title="Leonhard Euler">Leonhard Euler</a> introduced variable exponents, and, implicitly, non-integer exponents by writing:<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"consider exponentials or powers in which the exponent itself is a variable. It is clear that quantities of this kind are not <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_function" title="Algebraic function">algebraic functions</a>, since in those the exponents must be constant."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euler_1748_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Euler_1748-14">[14]</a></sup> </p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The expression <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup>2</sup> = <i>b</i> · <i>b</i></span> is called "the <a href="/wiki/Square_(algebra)" title="Square (algebra)">square</a> of <i>b</i>" or "<i>b</i> squared", because the area of a square with side-length <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i></span> is <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup>2</sup></span>.
</p><p>Similarly, the expression <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup>3</sup> = <i>b</i> · <i>b</i> · <i>b</i></span>  is called "the <a href="/wiki/Cube_(algebra)" title="Cube (algebra)">cube</a> of <i>b</i>" or "<i>b</i> cubed", because the volume of a cube with side-length <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i></span> is <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup>3</sup></span>.
</p><p>When it is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_integer" title="Positive integer">positive integer</a>, the exponent indicates how many copies of the base are multiplied together. For example, <span class="texhtml">3<sup>5</sup> = 3 · 3 · 3 · 3 · 3 = 243</span>. The base <span class="texhtml">3</span> appears <span class="texhtml">5</span> times in the multiplication, because the exponent is <span class="texhtml">5</span>. Here, <span class="texhtml">243</span> is the <i>5th power of 3</i>, or <i>3 raised to the 5th power</i>.
</p><p>The word "raised" is usually omitted, and sometimes "power" as well, so <span class="texhtml">3<sup>5</sup></span> can be simply read "3 to the 5th", or "3 to the 5". Therefore, the exponentiation <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span> can be expressed as "<i>b</i> to the power of <i>n</i>", "<i>b</i> to the <i>n</i>th power", "<i>b</i> to the <i>n</i>th", or most briefly as "<i>b</i> to the <i>n</i>".
</p><p>A formula with nested exponentiation, such as <span class="texhtml">3<sup>5<sup>7</sup></sup></span> (which means <span class="texhtml">3<sup>(5<sup>7</sup>)</sup></span> and not <span class="texhtml">(3<sup>5</sup>)<sup>7</sup></span>), is called a tower of powers, or simply a tower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Integer_exponents">Integer exponents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Integer exponents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The exponentiation operation with integer exponents may be defined directly from elementary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arithmetic_operation" title="Arithmetic operation">arithmetic operations</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Positive_exponents">Positive exponents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Positive exponents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The definition of the exponentiation as an iterated multiplication can be <a href="/wiki/Formal_proof" title="Formal proof">formalized</a> by using <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_induction" title="Mathematical induction">induction</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and this definition can be used as soon one has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associativity" title="Associativity">associative</a> multiplication:
</p><p>The base case is 
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{1}=b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zero_exponent">Zero exponent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Zero exponent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By definition, any nonzero number raised to the <span class="texhtml">0</span> power is <span class="texhtml">1</span>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{0}=1.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1.</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{0}=1.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{0}=1.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/de10f50a06d8e714f55212cadf1da761bcec4c1a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.96ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>This definition is the only possible that allows extending the formula
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{m+n}=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{m+n}=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{m+n}=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/259b25c515e091594d2f0ea2b75bf2628ce45f51" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:14.604ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>to zero exponents. It may be used in every <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_structure" title="Algebraic structure">algebraic structure</a> with a multiplication that has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiplicative_identity" title="Multiplicative identity">identity</a>.
</p><p>Intuitionally, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{0}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{0}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b^{0}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b5456c9d8bf077b24d003cf08da7a63403e24a8c" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.052ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> may be interpreted as the <a href="/wiki/Empty_product" title="Empty product">empty product</a> of copies of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span>. So, the equality <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{0}=1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{0}=1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b^{0}=1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/103471463029b683b437ab58d8ac1e7ec70a5023" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.313ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> is a special case of the general convention for the empty product.
</p><p>The case of <span class="texhtml">0<sup>0</sup></span> is more complicated. In contexts where only integer powers are considered, the value <span class="texhtml">1</span> is generally assigned to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 0^{0},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mn>0</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 0^{0},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle 0^{0},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9b394e60b04bd9b9c2c0da0cd0c467c2e2f17776" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.864ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> but, otherwise, the choice of whether to assign it a value and what value to assign may depend on context. <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033199720">.mw-parser-output div.crossreference{padding-left:0}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable crossreference" role="note">For more details, see <a href="/wiki/Zero_to_the_power_of_zero" title="Zero to the power of zero">Zero to the power of zero</a>.</span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Negative_exponents">Negative exponents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Negative exponents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Exponentiation with negative exponents is defined by the following identity, which holds for any integer <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> and nonzero <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{-n}={\frac {1}{b^{n}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{-n}={\frac {1}{b^{n}}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{-n}={\frac {1}{b^{n}}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/379fe0b14ea9aadbbe14631c373e5bdac0184feb" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:10.292ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">[1]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Raising 0 to a negative exponent is undefined but, in some circumstances, it may be interpreted as infinity (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \infty }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi mathvariant="normal">∞<!-- ∞ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \infty }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\infty " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c26c105004f30c27aa7c2a9c601550a4183b1f21" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.324ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>).
</p><p>This definition of exponentiation with negative exponents is the only one that allows extending the identity <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{m+n}=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>m</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>m</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{m+n}=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle b^{m+n}=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/259b25c515e091594d2f0ea2b75bf2628ce45f51" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:14.604ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> to negative exponents (consider the case <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle m=-n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>m</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m=-n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle m=-n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9d6e9afd09ef335f99a58a361faacfff3de778a5" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:8.342ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>).
</p><p>The same definition applies to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invertible_element" title="Invertible element">invertible elements</a> in a multiplicative <a href="/wiki/Monoid" title="Monoid">monoid</a>, that is, an <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_structure" title="Algebraic structure">algebraic structure</a>, with an associative multiplication and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiplicative_identity" title="Multiplicative identity">multiplicative identity</a> denoted <span class="texhtml">1</span> (for example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Square_matrices" title="Square matrices">square matrices</a> of a given dimension). In particular, in such a structure, the inverse of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invertible_element" title="Invertible element">invertible element</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is standardly denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x^{-1}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{-1}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x^{{-1}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a9d686441acca0e660bc3343d83f1083adfb3dc3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.309ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Identities_and_properties">Identities and properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Identities and properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Laws of Indices" redirects here. For the horse, see <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Indices_(horse)" title="Laws of Indices (horse)">Laws of Indices (horse)</a>.</div>
<p>The following <a href="/wiki/Identity_(mathematics)" title="Identity (mathematics)">identities</a>, often called <b><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1023754711">.mw-parser-output .vanchor>:target~.vanchor-text{background-color:#b1d2ff}</style><span class="vanchor"><span id="exponent_rules"></span><span class="vanchor-text">exponent rules</span></span></b>, hold for all integer exponents, provided that the base is non-zero:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-:1-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}b^{m+n}&amp;=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}\\\left(b^{m}\right)^{n}&amp;=b^{m\cdot n}\\(b\cdot c)^{n}&amp;=b^{n}\cdot c^{n}\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}b^{m+n}&amp;=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}\\\left(b^{m}\right)^{n}&amp;=b^{m\cdot n}\\(b\cdot c)^{n}&amp;=b^{n}\cdot c^{n}\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}b^{m+n}&amp;=b^{m}\cdot b^{n}\\\left(b^{m}\right)^{n}&amp;=b^{m\cdot n}\\(b\cdot c)^{n}&amp;=b^{n}\cdot c^{n}\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9e1b35cff2d627e5830a2441b5611f1fc0f8ccfc" style="vertical-align: -4.005ex; width:17.129ex; height:9.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Unlike addition and multiplication, exponentiation is not <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commutative" title="Commutative">commutative</a>. For example, <span class="texhtml">2<sup>3</sup> = 8 ≠ 3<sup>2</sup> = 9</span>.  Also unlike addition and multiplication, exponentiation is not <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associative" title="Associative">associative</a>. For example, <span class="texhtml">(2<sup>3</sup>)<sup>2</sup> = 8<sup>2</sup> = 64</span>, whereas <span class="texhtml">2<sup>(3<sup>2</sup>)</sup> = 2<sup>9</sup> = 512</span>. Without parentheses, the conventional <a href="/wiki/Order_of_operations" title="Order of operations">order of operations</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serial_exponentiation" title="Serial exponentiation">serial exponentiation</a> in superscript notation is top-down (or <i>right</i>-associative), not bottom-up<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson_1958_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson_1958-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bronstein_1987_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bronstein_1987-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIST_2010_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIST_2010-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zeidler_2013_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zeidler_2013-21">[21]</a></sup> (or <i>left</i>-associative). That is, 
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b^{p^{q}}=b^{\left(p^{q}\right)},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<p>which, in general, is different from 
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \left(b^{p}\right)^{q}=b^{pq}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>q</mi>

</mstyle>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \left(b^{p}\right)^{q}=b^{pq}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \left(b^{p}\right)^{q}=b^{pq}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/78911e3a5a6f894fdf2828cd6a7ad0db640d738d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.413ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_of_a_sum">Powers of a sum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Powers of a sum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The powers of a sum can normally be computed from the powers of the summands by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binomial_formula" title="Binomial formula">binomial formula</a>
</p>

<mo>!</mo>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>!</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>!</mo>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (a+b)^{n}=\sum _{i=0}^{n}{\binom {n}{i}}a^{i}b^{n-i}=\sum _{i=0}^{n}{\frac {n!}{i!(n-i)!}}a^{i}b^{n-i}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle (a+b)^{n}=\sum _{i=0}^{n}{\binom {n}{i}}a^{i}b^{n-i}=\sum _{i=0}^{n}{\frac {n!}{i!(n-i)!}}a^{i}b^{n-i}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3d288a32615a5b91dc0060530c3df1721a6fa7ac" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:49.201ex; height:6.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>However, this formula is true only if the summands commute (i.e. that <span class="texhtml"><i>ab</i> = <i>ba</i></span>), which is implied if they belong to a <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_structure" title="Algebraic structure">structure</a> that is <a href="/wiki/Commutative_property" title="Commutative property">commutative</a>. Otherwise, if <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">a</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span> are, say, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Square_matrices" title="Square matrices">square matrices</a> of the same size, this formula cannot be used. It follows that in <a href="/wiki/Computer_algebra" title="Computer algebra">computer algebra</a>, many <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithms</a> involving integer exponents must be changed when the exponentiation bases do not commute. Some general purpose <a href="/wiki/Computer_algebra_system" title="Computer algebra system">computer algebra systems</a> use a different notation (sometimes <span class="texhtml">^^</span> instead of <span class="texhtml">^</span>) for exponentiation with non-commuting bases, which is then called <b>non-commutative exponentiation</b>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Combinatorial_interpretation">Combinatorial interpretation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Combinatorial interpretation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="#Exponentiation_over_sets">Exponentiation over sets</a></div>
<p>For nonnegative integers <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span>, the value of <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i><sup><i>m</i></sup></span> is the number of <a href="/wiki/Function_(mathematics)" title="Function (mathematics)">functions</a> from a <a href="/wiki/Set_(mathematics)" title="Set (mathematics)">set</a> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span> elements to a set of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> elements (see <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_number#Cardinal_exponentiation" title="Cardinal number">cardinal exponentiation</a>). Such functions can be represented as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span>-<a href="/wiki/Tuple" title="Tuple">tuples</a> from an <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>-element set (or as <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span>-letter words from an <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>-letter alphabet).  Some examples for particular values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> are given in the following table:
</p>
<dl><dd><table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<th><span class="texhtml"><i>n</i><sup><i>m</i></sup></span>
</th>
<th>The <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i><sup><i>m</i></sup></span> possible <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">m</span>-tuples of elements from the set <span class="texhtml">{1, ..., <i>n</i>}</span>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>0<sup>5</sup> = 0
</td>
<td class="table-cast" style="background: #ECECEC; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;">none
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>1<sup>4</sup> = 1
</td>
<td>(1, 1, 1, 1)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>2<sup>3</sup> = 8
</td>
<td>(1, 1, 1), (1, 1, 2), (1, 2, 1), (1, 2, 2), (2, 1, 1), (2, 1, 2), (2, 2, 1), (2, 2, 2)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>3<sup>2</sup> = 9
</td>
<td>(1, 1), (1, 2), (1, 3), (2, 1), (2, 2), (2, 3), (3, 1), (3, 2), (3, 3)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>4<sup>1</sup> = 4
</td>
<td>(1), (2), (3), (4)
</td></tr>

</td>

</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Particular_bases">Particular bases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Particular bases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_of_ten"><span class="anchor" id="Base_10"></span>Powers of ten</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Powers of ten">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scientific_notation" title="Scientific notation">Scientific notation</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Power_of_10" title="Power of 10">Power of 10</a></div>
<p>In the base ten (<a href="/wiki/Decimal" title="Decimal">decimal</a>) number system, integer powers of <span class="texhtml">10</span> are written as the digit <span class="texhtml">1</span> followed or preceded by a number of zeroes determined by the sign and magnitude of the exponent.  For example, <span class="texhtml"><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003100000000000000♠"></span>10<sup>3</sup></span> = <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003100000000000000♠"></span>1000</span></span> and <span class="texhtml"><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="6996100000000000000♠"></span>10<sup>−4</sup></span> = <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="6996100000000000000♠"></span>0.0001</span></span>.
</p><p>Exponentiation with base <span class="texhtml"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/10_(number)" title="10 (number)">10</a></span> is used in <a href="/wiki/Scientific_notation" title="Scientific notation">scientific notation</a> to denote large or small numbers. For instance, <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7008299792458000000♠"></span>299<span style="margin-left:.25em;">792</span><span style="margin-left:.25em;">458</span> m/s</span> (the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a> in vacuum, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metres_per_second" title="Metres per second">metres per second</a>) can be written as <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7008299792458000000♠"></span>2.997<span style="margin-left:.25em;">924</span><span style="margin-left:.25em;">58</span><span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>8</sup> m/s</span> and then <a href="/wiki/Approximation" title="Approximation">approximated</a> as <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7008299800000000000♠"></span>2.998<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>8</sup> m/s</span>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_prefix" title="SI prefix">SI prefixes</a> based on powers of <span class="texhtml">10</span> are also used to describe small or large quantities. For example, the prefix <a href="/wiki/Kilo-" title="Kilo-">kilo</a> means <span class="texhtml"><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003100000000000000♠"></span>10<sup>3</sup></span> = <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003100000000000000♠"></span>1000</span></span>, so a kilometre is <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7003100000000000000♠"></span>1000 m</span>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_of_two"><span class="anchor" id="Base_2"></span>Powers of two</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Powers of two">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Power_of_two" title="Power of two">Power of two</a></div>
<p>The first negative powers of <span class="texhtml">2</span> are commonly used, and have special names, e.g.: <i><a href="/wiki/One_half" title="One half">half</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4_(number)" title="4 (number)">quarter</a></i>.
</p><p>Powers of <span class="texhtml">2</span> appear in <a href="/wiki/Set_theory" title="Set theory">set theory</a>, since a set with <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> members has a <a href="/wiki/Power_set" title="Power set">power set</a>, the set of all of its <a href="/wiki/Subset" title="Subset">subsets</a>, which has <span class="texhtml">2<sup><i>n</i></sup></span> members.
</p><p>Integer powers of <span class="texhtml">2</span> are important in <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>. The positive integer powers <span class="texhtml">2<sup><i>n</i></sup></span> give the number of possible values for an <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>-<a href="/wiki/Bit" title="Bit">bit</a> integer <a href="/wiki/Binary_number" title="Binary number">binary number</a>; for example, a <a href="/wiki/Byte" title="Byte">byte</a> may take <span class="texhtml">2<sup>8</sup> = 256</span> different values. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binary_number_system" title="Binary number system">binary number system</a> expresses any number as a sum of powers of <span class="texhtml">2</span>, and denotes it as a sequence of <span class="texhtml">0</span> and <span class="texhtml">1</span>, separated by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binary_point" title="Binary point">binary point</a>, where <span class="texhtml">1</span> indicates a power of <span class="texhtml">2</span> that appears in the sum; the exponent is determined by the place of this <span class="texhtml">1</span>: the nonnegative exponents are the rank of the <span class="texhtml">1</span> on the left of the point (starting from <span class="texhtml">0</span>), and the negative exponents are determined by the rank on the right of the point.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_of_one">Powers of one</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Powers of one">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The powers of one are all one: <span class="texhtml">1<sup><i>n</i></sup> = 1</span>.
</p><p>The first power of a number is the number itself: <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n^{1}=n.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>n</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n^{1}=n.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle n^{1}=n.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0e923ce1f3719a339fdffb5bbd45af6c74f1b86f" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.589ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_of_zero">Powers of zero</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Powers of zero">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>If the exponent <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> is positive (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> &gt; 0</span>), the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th power of zero is zero: <span class="texhtml">0<sup><i>n</i></sup> = 0</span>.
</p><p>If the exponent <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span> is negative (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> &lt; 0</span>), the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th power of zero <span class="texhtml">0<sup><i>n</i></sup></span> is undefined, because it must equal <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 1/0^{-n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mn>0</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 1/0^{-n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle 1/0^{-n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/931515a5767d401c076dd11dbaf0453ea6c3c2d3" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:5.984ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> with <span class="texhtml">−<i>n</i> &gt; 0</span>, and this would be <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 1/0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mn>1</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mn>0</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 1/0}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="1/0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5d6c2a431df105fb423ded3679bfd7104af53fa5" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.487ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> according to above.
</p><p>The expression <a href="/wiki/Zero_to_the_power_of_zero" title="Zero to the power of zero"><span class="texhtml">0<sup>0</sup></span></a> is either defined as 1, or it is left undefined.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Powers_of_negative_one">Powers of negative one</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Powers of negative one">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>If <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is an even integer, then <span class="texhtml">(−1)<sup><i>n</i></sup> = 1</span>.
</p><p>If <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is an odd integer, then <span class="texhtml">(−1)<sup><i>n</i></sup> = −1</span>.
</p><p>Because of this, powers of <span class="texhtml">−1</span> are useful for expressing alternating <a href="/wiki/Sequence" title="Sequence">sequences</a>.  For a similar discussion of powers of the complex number <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i></span>, see <a href="#Powers_of_complex_numbers">§ Powers of complex numbers</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Large_exponents">Large exponents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Large exponents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_sequence" title="Limit of a sequence">limit of a sequence</a> of powers of a number greater than one diverges; in other words, the sequence grows without bound:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup> → ∞</span> as <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> → ∞</span> when <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i> &gt; 1</span></dd></dl>
<p>This can be read as "<i>b</i> to the power of <i>n</i> tends to <a href="/wiki/Extended_real_number_line" title="Extended real number line">+∞</a> as <i>n</i> tends to infinity when <i>b</i> is greater than one".
</p><p>Powers of a number with <a href="/wiki/Absolute_value" title="Absolute value">absolute value</a> less than one tend to zero:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup> → 0</span> as <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> → ∞</span> when <span class="texhtml">|<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em;"><i>b</i></span>| &lt; 1</span></dd></dl>
<p>Any power of one is always one:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup> = 1</span> for all <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> if <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i> = 1</span></dd></dl>
<p>Powers of <span class="texhtml">–1</span> alternate between <span class="texhtml">1</span> and <span class="texhtml">–1</span> as <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> alternates between even and odd, and thus do not tend to any limit as <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> grows.
</p><p>If <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i> &lt; –1</span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i><sup><i>n</i></sup></span> alternates between larger and larger positive and negative numbers as <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> alternates between even and odd, and thus does not tend to any limit as <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> grows.
</p><p>If the exponentiated number varies while tending to <span class="texhtml">1</span> as the exponent tends to infinity, then the limit is not necessarily one of those above. A particularly important case is
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="texhtml">(1 + 1/<i>n</i>)<sup><i>n</i></sup> → <i>e</i></span> as <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> → ∞</span></dd></dl>
<p>See <i><a href="#The_exponential_function">§ The exponential function</a></i> below.
</p><p>Other limits, in particular those of expressions that take on an <a href="/wiki/Indeterminate_form" title="Indeterminate form">indeterminate form</a>, are described in <a href="#Limits_of_powers">§ Limits of powers</a> below.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_functions">Power functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exponentiation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Power functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle f(-x)=-f(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle f(-x)=-f(x)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b022ffe516cf5bc26a68fd954753aa2bddf508f1" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.55ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>)</span> are called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odd_functions" title="Odd functions">odd functions</a>.
</p><p>For <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c&lt;0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>c</mi>
<mo>&lt;</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c&lt;0}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c &lt; 0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/26a48dc798956117afd8c429c39886678c0e7204" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.268ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, the opposite asymptotic behavior is true in each case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calculus:_Early_Transcendentals_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Calculus:_Early_Transcendentals-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
